System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To make an informed decision about which route to choose in the traffic network game, let's consider the costs associated with each route and how they might change based on the choices of other participants.

1. **Routes and Cost Functions:**
   - Route O-L-D: The cost is \(10X + 210\), where \(X\) is the number of participants choosing this route.
   - Route O-R-D: The cost is \(210 + 10Y\), where \(Y\) is the number of participants choosing this route.

2. **Objective:** 
   - The goal is to minimize travel costs to maximize the payoff each round.

3. **Initial Analysis:**
   - If I am the only one choosing route O-L-D, the cost would be \(10 \times 1 + 210 = 220\).
   - If I am the only one choosing route O-R-D, the cost would be \(210 + 10 \times 1 = 220\).
   - In both cases, the costs are equal, assuming no other participants choose the same route as me.

4. **Considering Other Participants:**
   - If the majority chooses route O-L-D, the cost of route O-R-D may be lower and vice versa. 
   - Since there are 18 participants, evenly distributed choices would result in 9 participants on each route.
   - For O-L-D: \(10 \times 9 + 210 = 300\)
   - For O-R-D: \(210 + 10 \times 9 = 300\)
   - The costs are equal with an even distribution.

5. **Strategy:**
   - If the previous round results indicated that more participants chose one specific route, opting for the less chosen route in the following round could lower costs.
   - With a tendency to balance the number choosing between O-L-D and O-R-D, starting with O-R-D might be a slightly safer bet, assuming others also notice that O-R-D initially has a constant segment cost without dependency at the start.

Based on the analysis:
- I would start by choosing route "O-R-D", considering there could be an advantage if many participants are uncertain and gravitate towards choosing O-L-D to avoid the variable cost at the L-D segment initially. 

```json
{
    "route": "O-R-D"
}
```

1. **Outcome of Previous Round:**
   - Since the regret was 0, it suggests that the costs on both routes could have been equal or O-R-D was the less costly path compared to O-L-D.
   - This implies that a substantial number of participants likely chose O-L-D, making its cost greater or equal to O-R-D.

2. **Analysis of Expected Costs for Current Round:**
   - If many participants saw no regret in choosing O-R-D, they might continue choosing O-R-D, resulting in higher costs for it in this round.
   - O-L-D might be less costly this round if participants shift due to previous results, thereby increasing the congestion and cost on O-R-D.

3. **Making the Choice:**
   - Given that my regret was 0, sticking with O-R-D seems initially reasonable if status remains quo.
   - However, predicting how others might react to their outcomes (if many experienced high costs) should also influence the decision.
   - If I anticipate others shifting to O-L-D due to results, sticking with O-R-D could remain optimal if the cost dynamics tilt favorably.

4. **Decision:** 
   - Weighing the possibility of participants shifting routes due to previous congestion, there could be a strategic advantage in maintaining the choice of O-R-D if it's not apparent that everyone experienced similar zero regret.
   - Therefore, a continued choice of O-R-D might balance maximizing payoff while monitoring participants' behavior in subsequent rounds.

Based on the analysis, and considering changes in participant choices will gradually impact the best path over time:

```json
    "route": "O-R-D"
```

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```

   - Cost: \(10X + 210\)

   - If many drivers choose this route, the cost will increase due to congestion on segment O-L.

   - This involves the variable cost segment O-L, the free segment L-R, and variable cost segment R-D.

3. **Route O-R-D:**

   - If fewer participants choose this route, it might be advantageous due to its initial higher fixed cost but potentially lower congestion costs.

4. **Determine Initial Choice:**
   - With balanced assumptions and minor expectations for volatility and participant shift, attempting O-L-R-D might initially maximize the potential for adaptability while observing congestion impacts.

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```


Human: The available routes are: O-L-D, O-R-D.
Think step-by-step before making your decision.

LLM Output: To decide which route to take, let's analyze the available options step-by-step to maximize our payoff by minimizing the cost:

### Routes and Cost Structure
1. **Route O-L-D:**
   - Cost: \(10X + 210\)
     - \(X\) is the number of participants choosing O-L-D.
     - Variable component: Congestion can increase the cost linearly with the number of participants.

2. **Route O-R-D:**
   - Cost: \(210 + 10Y\)
     - \(Y\) is the number of participants choosing O-R-D.
     - The travel cost component \(10Y\) depends on the number of participants traveling the segment R-D.

### Analyzing Participant Behavior:
- If many choose O-L-D, its cost rises due to congestion in the O-L segment.
- If many choose O-R-D, its cost rises due to congestion in the R-D segment.

### Strategy:
1. **Equal Distribution:**
   - If participants evenly distribute, costs tend to balance around both routes. For instance, with a distribution of 9 on each:
     - O-L-D: \(10 \times 9 + 210 = 300\)
     - O-R-D: \(210 + 10 \times 9 = 300\)

2. **Imbalance Consideration:**
   - Consider choosing a less chosen path if a past pattern indicates a high cost on one route due to high selection.

3. **Initial Choice Guidance:**
   - If a history or prediction indicates a bias (e.g., more people typically choose O-L-D thinking it strategizes better), then O-R-D can be preferred assuming it might be less congested.

### Initial Decision:
- For balance, or if no past data suggests an imbalance, opting for O-R-D might be strategic to start based on inherent structure stability unless prior rounds drastically changed dynamics.

Here's the route choice for this round:

```json
{
    "route": "O-R-D"
}
```

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```

LLM Output: To make a strategic decision about the route choice, we need to consider the cost dynamics associated with each route and how participant distribution affects these costs. Here are the steps to follow:

### Route Options and Cost Structure

1. **Route O-L-D:**
   - Cost: \(10X + 210\)
   - Travel through O-L, which has a variable cost depending on the number of participants, plus a fixed cost for L-D.

2. **Route O-L-R-D:**
   - Cost: \(10X + (10Y)\)
   - Involves traveling O-L with its associated variable cost and them moving across L-R for free before reaching R-D, which has an additional variable cost.
   - Optimal if O-L and R-D segments are not overly congested.

3. **Route O-R-D:**
   - Cost: \(210 + 10Y\)
   - Fixed cost for O-R, then variable cost for R-D.

### Analyzing Participant Impact and Strategy:

1. **Assess the Likely Behavior:**
   - If most participants focus on one route, congestion decreases the attractiveness of that route.
   - Check past behaviors, if known, to predict possible shifts.

2. **Balanced Distribution Analysis:**
   - O-R-D might become less congested if prior rounds had high participants due to perception of stability from its fixed start cost.
   - O-L-D might have congestion as it tends to attract participants avoiding fixed upfront costs.
   - O-L-R-D offers adaptive balance, leveraging the no-cost L-R and managing O-L and R-D depending on traffic.

3. **Strategic Choice:**
   - If unsure of significant shifts, O-L-R-D can be ideal due to its mid-ground strategy, potentially offering a lower combined cost by splitting the travel across critical segments effectively.
   - Adjust if patterns suggest overloading on this path specifically.

**Decision:**

Given no prior imbalance indication or clear trend, employ a balanced approach. Opt for O-L-R-D initially, adapting based on observed participant behavior in future rounds.

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 2 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 2 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
If you happen to be the only driver who chooses route O-L-D, and all other 17 drivers choose route O-R-D, then your travel cost from point O to point D is equal to (10 x 1) + 210 = 220.
If, on another round, you and 2 more drivers choose route O-R-D and 15 other drivers choose route O-L-D, then your travel cost for that round will be 210 + (10 x 3) = 240.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```

2. **Route O-R-D:**

     - \(Y\) represents the number of participants choosing this route.
     - Costs increase with the number of participants choosing the R-D segment.

System Message: 
You will be participating in an experiment on route selection in traffic networks.
During this experiment you'll be asked to make many decisions about route selection in a traffic network game.
Your payoff will depend on the decisions you make as well as the decisions made by the other participants.

There are 18 participants in this experiment, including yourself, who will be asked to serve as drivers and choose a route to travel in a traffic network game that is described below.
You will play the game for 40 identical rounds.

Consider the very simple traffic network described below.
Nodes:
O L R D
Segments and associated costs:
Segment O-L, cost function: 10 * X
Segment O-R, cost function: 210
Segment L-D, cost function: 210
Segment L-R, cost function: 0
Segment R-D, cost function: 10 * X
Each driver is required to choose one of 3 routes to travel from the starting point, denoted by O, to the final destination, denoted by D.
There are 3 alternative routes and they are denoted by ['O-L-D', 'O-L-R-D', 'O-R-D']. 

Travel is always costly in terms of the time needed to complete a segment of the road, tolls, fuel etc.
The travel costs are written near each segment of the route you choose.
For example, if you choose route O-L-D, you will be charged a total cost of 10X + 210 where X indicates the number of participants who choose segment O-L to travel from O to L plus a fixed cost of 210 for traveling on segment L-D.
Similarly, if you choose route O-R-D, you will be charged a total travel cost of 210 + 10Y, where Y indicates the number of participants who choose the segment R-D to drive from O to D.
Please note that the cost charged for segments O-L and R-D depends on the number of drivers choosing them.
In contrast, the cost charged for traveling on segments L-D and O-R is fixed at 210 and does not depend on the number of drivers choosing them.
All the drivers make their route choices independently of one another and leave point O at the same time.

Example.
Supposing that you choose route O-L-R-D, 3 other drivers choose route O-L-D, and 14 additional drivers choose route O-R-D.
Then, your total travel cost for that period is equal to (10 x 4) + 0 + (10 x 14) = 180.
Note that in this example, 4 drivers (including you) traveled on the segment O-L and 14 drivers (again, including you) traveled the segment R-D to go from O to D.
Each of the 3 drivers choosing route O-L-D will be charged a travel cost of (10 x 4) + 210 = 250.
Each of the 14 drivers choosing the route O-R-D will be charged a travel cost of 210 + (10 x 14) = 350.

At the beginning of each round, you will receive an endowment of 400 points.
Your payoff for each round will be determined by subtracting your travel cost from your endowment.
Your goal is to maximize your payoff (likewise minimize your cost).
All 40 rounds have exactly the same structure.

The output should be formatted as a JSON instance that conforms to the JSON schema below.

As an example, for the schema {"properties": {"foo": {"title": "Foo", "description": "a list of strings", "type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}}, "required": ["foo"]}
the object {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]} is a well-formatted instance of the schema. The object {"properties": {"foo": ["bar", "baz"]}} is not well-formatted.

Here is the output schema:
```
{"properties": {"route": {"title": "Route", "description": "choice of route", "type": "string"}}, "required": ["route"]}
```

### Route Options and Cost Structures

1. **Route O-L-D:**

   - Costs vary depending on the number of participants on the O-L segment.
   - Optimal if O-L is less congested.

2. **Route O-L-R-D:**
   - Cost: \(10X + 10Y\)
   - Includes the variable cost of O-L and R-D segments, but has a zero-cost L-R segment.
   - Offers flexibility and can be cost-effective if both segments aren't heavily congested.

3. **Route O-R-D:**
   - Cost: \(210 + 10Y\)
   - Has a fixed cost for the O-R segment and variable cost for R-D.
   - Stable choice if R-D segment remains less congested.

### Analyzing Participant Dynamics and Strategy

1. **Traffic Dynamics:**
   - Common player predictions and past choices can influence congestion: more on a route increases costs.
   - Drivers avoid high congestion; thus, routes less chosen previously might be more attractive now.

   - Consider O-R-D if the congestion on O-L becomes significant, causing participants to abandon that path.
